   <h1 id="firstHeading" class="firstHeading">Samoa</h1> 
   <div id="bodyContent" class="vector-body"> 
    <div id="siteSub" class="noprint">
     From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia
    </div> 
    <div id="contentSub"></div> 
    <div id="contentSub2"></div> 
    <div id="jump-to-nav"></div> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#mw-head">Jump to navigation</a> <a class="mw-jump-link" href="#searchInput">Jump to search</a> 
    <div id="mw-content-text" class="mw-body-content mw-content-ltr" lang="en" dir="ltr">
     <div class="mw-parser-output">
      <div class="shortdescription nomobile noexcerpt noprint searchaux" style="display:none">
       Polynesian island country
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       This article is about the nation of Samoa. For the geographical region, see <a href="/wiki/Samoan_Islands" title="Samoan Islands">Samoan Islands</a>. For the Samoan United States territory, see <a href="/wiki/American_Samoa" title="American Samoa">American Samoa</a>. For other uses, see <a href="/wiki/Samoa_(disambiguation)" class="mw-disambig" title="Samoa (disambiguation)">Samoa (disambiguation)</a>.
      </div>

      <p><b>Samoa</b> (<span class="rt-commentedText nowrap"><span class="IPA nopopups noexcerpt"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA/English" title="Help:IPA/English">/<span style="border-bottom:1px dotted"><span title="'s' in 'sigh'">s</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span><span title="/ˈ/: primary stress follows">ˈ</span><span title="'m' in 'my'">m</span><span title="/oʊ/: 'o' in 'code'">oʊ</span><span title="/ə/: 'a' in 'about'">ə</span></span>/</a></span></span>), officially the <b>Independent State of</b> <b>Samoa</b> (<a href="/wiki/Samoan_language" title="Samoan language">Samoan</a>: <i lang="sm">Malo Saʻoloto Tutoʻatasi o Sāmoa</i>; <a href="/wiki/Samoan_language" title="Samoan language">Samoan</a>: <i lang="sm">Sāmoa</i>, <small>IPA:&nbsp;</small><span title="Representation in the International Phonetic Alphabet (IPA)" class="IPA"><a href="/wiki/Help:IPA" title="Help:IPA">[ˈsaːmoa]</a></span>) and until 1997 known as <b>Western Samoa</b>, is a <a href="/wiki/Polynesia" title="Polynesia">Polynesian</a> <a href="/wiki/Island_country" title="Island country">island country</a> consisting of two main islands (<a href="/wiki/Savai%27i" class="mw-redirect" title="Savai'i">Savai'i</a> and <a href="/wiki/Upolu" title="Upolu">Upolu</a>), two smaller, inhabited islands (<a href="/wiki/Manono_Island" title="Manono Island">Manono</a> and <a href="/wiki/Apolima" title="Apolima">Apolima</a>), and several smaller, uninhabited islands, including the <a href="/wiki/Aleipata_Islands" title="Aleipata Islands">Aleipata Islands</a> (<a href="/wiki/Nu%27utele" class="mw-redirect" title="Nu'utele">Nu'utele</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nu%27ulua" class="mw-redirect" title="Nu'ulua">Nu'ulua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Fanuatapu" title="Fanuatapu">Fanuatapu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Namua" title="Namua">Namua</a>). The capital city is <a href="/wiki/Apia" title="Apia">Apia</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Lapita_culture" title="Lapita culture">Lapita</a> people discovered and settled the <a href="/wiki/Samoan_Islands" title="Samoan Islands">Samoan Islands</a> around 3,500 years ago. They developed a <a href="/wiki/Samoan_language" title="Samoan language">Samoan language</a> and <a href="/wiki/Samoan_culture" title="Samoan culture">Samoan cultural identity</a>. </p>
      <p>Samoa is a <a href="/wiki/Unitary_state" title="Unitary state">unitary</a> <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary democracy</a> with <a href="/wiki/Administrative_divisions_of_Samoa" class="mw-redirect" title="Administrative divisions of Samoa">eleven administrative divisions</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Sovereign_state" title="Sovereign state">sovereign state</a> is a member of the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a> as a <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_republic" class="mw-redirect" title="Commonwealth republic">Commonwealth republic</a>. Western Samoa was admitted to the <a href="/wiki/Member_states_of_the_United_Nations#Current_members" title="Member states of the United Nations">United Nations</a> on 15 December 1976.<sup id="cite_ref-UN_8-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-UN-8">[8]</a></sup> Because of the Samoans' seafaring skills, pre-20th-century European explorers referred to the entire <a href="/wiki/Island_group" class="mw-redirect" title="Island group">island group</a> (which includes <a href="/wiki/American_Samoa" title="American Samoa">American Samoa</a>) as the "Navigator Islands.”<sup id="cite_ref-9" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-CC_10-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CC-10">[10]</a></sup> The country was occupied by the German Empire from 1899 to 1915, and by a joint British and New Zealand colonial administration until 1 January 1962, when it became independent. </p>

      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="History">History</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Samoa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: History">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/History_of_Samoa" title="History of Samoa">History of Samoa</a>
      </div> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_Samoa">Early Samoa</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Samoa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early Samoa">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Samoa was discovered and settled by the Samoans’ Lapita ancestors (Austronesian people who spoke <a href="/wiki/Oceanic_languages" title="Oceanic languages">Oceanic languages</a>). New Zealand scientists have dated the earliest human remains found in Samoa to between roughly 2900 and 3500 years ago. The remains were discovered at a <a href="/wiki/Lapita_culture" title="Lapita culture">Lapita</a> site at <a href="/wiki/Mulifanua" title="Mulifanua">Mulifanua</a>, and the scientists’ findings were published in 1974.<sup id="cite_ref-green_11-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-green-11">[11]</a></sup> The Samoans’ origins have been studied in modern times through scientific research on Polynesian <a href="/wiki/Genetics" title="Genetics">genetics</a>, <a href="/wiki/Linguistics" title="Linguistics">linguistics</a> and <a href="/wiki/Anthropology" title="Anthropology">anthropology</a>. Although this research is ongoing, a number of theories have been proposed. One theory is that the original Samoans were <a href="/wiki/Austronesian_peoples" title="Austronesian peoples">Austronesians</a> who arrived during a final period of eastward expansion of the Lapita peoples out of Southeast Asia and <a href="/wiki/Melanesia" title="Melanesia">Melanesia</a> between 2,500 and 1,500 BCE.<sup id="cite_ref-12" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Intimate sociocultural and genetic ties were maintained between Samoa, Fiji, and Tonga, and the archaeological record supports oral tradition and native genealogies that indicate inter-island voyaging and intermarriage between pre-colonial Samoans, Fijians, and Tongans. Notable figures in Samoan history included the <a href="/wiki/Tui_Manu%27a" title="Tui Manu'a">Tui Manu'a</a> line, Queen <a href="/wiki/Salamasina" title="Salamasina">Salamasina</a>, <a href="/wiki/Falefa" title="Falefa">King Fonoti</a> and the four tama-a-aiga: <a href="/wiki/Malietoa" title="Malietoa">Malietoa</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tupua_Tamasese" title="Tupua Tamasese">Tupua Tamasese</a>, <a href="/wiki/Mata%27afa" class="mw-redirect" title="Mata'afa">Mata'afa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tuimalealiifano_Va%27aletoa_Sualauvi_II" title="Tuimalealiifano Va'aletoa Sualauvi II">Tuimalealiifano</a>. <a href="/wiki/Nafanua" title="Nafanua">Nafanua</a> was a famous woman warrior who was deified in ancient Samoan religion and whose patronage was highly sought after by successive Samoan rulers.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_13-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-13">[13]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Today, all of Samoa is united under its two principal royal families: the Sā Malietoa of the ancient Malietoa lineage that defeated the Tongans in the 13th century; and the Sā Tupua, Queen Salamasina's descendants and heirs who ruled Samoa in the centuries that followed her reign. Within these two principal lineages are the four highest titles of Samoa - the elder titles of Malietoa and Tupua Tamasese of antiquity as well as the newer Mata'afa and Tuimalealiifano titles who rose to prominence in 19th century wars that preceded the colonial period.<sup id="cite_ref-:1_13-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:1-13">[13]</a></sup> These four titles form the apex of the Samoan matai system as it stands today. </p>
      <p>Contact with Europeans began in the early 18th century. <a href="/wiki/Jacob_Roggeveen" title="Jacob Roggeveen">Jacob Roggeveen</a>, a Dutchman, was the first known non-Polynesian to sight the Samoan islands in 1722. This visit was followed by French explorer <a href="/wiki/Louis-Antoine_de_Bougainville" class="mw-redirect" title="Louis-Antoine de Bougainville">Louis-Antoine de Bougainville</a>, who named them the <i>Navigator Islands</i> in 1768. Contact was limited before the 1830s, which is when English <a href="/wiki/Missionaries" class="mw-redirect" title="Missionaries">missionaries</a>, whalers and traders began arriving.<sup id="cite_ref-14" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Samoa_in_the_1800s">Samoa in the 1800s</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Samoa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Samoa in the 1800s">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Visits by American trading and <a href="/wiki/Whaling" title="Whaling">whaling</a> vessels were important in the early economic development of Samoa. The <a href="/wiki/Salem,_Connecticut" title="Salem, Connecticut">Salem</a> brig <i>Roscoe</i> (Captain Benjamin Vanderford), in October 1821, was the first American trading vessel known to have called, and the <i>Maro</i> (Captain Richard Macy) of <a href="/wiki/Nantucket" title="Nantucket">Nantucket</a>, in 1824, was the first recorded United States whaler at Samoa.<sup id="cite_ref-15" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> The whalers came for fresh drinking water, firewood and provisions, and later, they recruited local men to serve as crewmen on their ships. The last recorded whaler visitor was the <i>Governor Morton</i> in 1870.<sup id="cite_ref-16" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Christian missionary work in Samoa began in 1830 when <a href="/wiki/John_Williams_(missionary)" title="John Williams (missionary)">John Williams</a> of the <a href="/wiki/London_Missionary_Society" title="London Missionary Society">London Missionary Society</a> arrived in <a href="/wiki/Sapapali%27i" class="mw-redirect" title="Sapapali'i">Sapapali'i</a> from the <a href="/wiki/Cook_Islands" title="Cook Islands">Cook Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tahiti" title="Tahiti">Tahiti</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-17" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup> According to Barbara A. West, "The Samoans were also known to engage in ‘headhunting', a ritual of war in which a warrior took the head of his slain opponent to give to his leader, thus proving his bravery."<sup id="cite_ref-18" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup> </p>
      <p> In <i><a href="/wiki/A_Footnote_to_History:_Eight_Years_of_Trouble_in_Samoa" title="A Footnote to History: Eight Years of Trouble in Samoa">A Footnote to History: Eight Years of Trouble in Samoa</a></i> (1892) <a href="/wiki/Robert_Louis_Stevenson" title="Robert Louis Stevenson">Robert Louis Stevenson</a>, details the activities of the <a href="/wiki/Great_power" title="Great power">great powers</a> battling for influence in Samoa – the United States, Germany and Britain – and the political machinations of the various Samoan factions within their indigenous political system.<sup id="cite_ref-rlssite_19-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-rlssite-19">[19]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-:0_20-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-20">[20]</a></sup> Even as they descended into ever greater interclan warfare, what most alarmed Stevenson was the Samoans' economic innocence. In 1894 just months before his death, he addressed the island chiefs:</p>
      <blockquote>
       <p>There is but one way to defend Samoa. Hear it before it is too late. It is to make roads, and gardens, and care for your trees, and sell their produce wisely, and, in one word, to occupy and use your country... if you do not occupy and use your country, others will. It will not continue to be yours or your children’s, if you occupy it for nothing. You and your children will in that case be cast out into outer darkness".</p>
      </blockquote>
      <p> He had "seen these judgments of God," in Hawaii where abandoned native churches stood like tombstones "over a grave, in the midst of the white men’s sugar fields".<sup id="cite_ref-21" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup> </p>
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:3_Samoan_girls_making_ava_1909.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/3_Samoan_girls_making_ava_1909.jpg/220px-3_Samoan_girls_making_ava_1909.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="143" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/3_Samoan_girls_making_ava_1909.jpg/330px-3_Samoan_girls_making_ava_1909.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3f/3_Samoan_girls_making_ava_1909.jpg/440px-3_Samoan_girls_making_ava_1909.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2164" data-file-height="1410"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">

        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Urville-Apia-public.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Urville-Apia-public.jpg/220px-Urville-Apia-public.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Urville-Apia-public.jpg/330px-Urville-Apia-public.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b6/Urville-Apia-public.jpg/440px-Urville-Apia-public.jpg 2x" data-file-width="700" data-file-height="497"></a>

         <div class="magnify">

         </div>Interior of Samoan house, Apia, Urville 1842.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Robert_Louis_Stevenson_birthday_fete,_Samoa_1896.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Robert_Louis_Stevenson_birthday_fete%2C_Samoa_1896.jpg/220px-Robert_Louis_Stevenson_birthday_fete%2C_Samoa_1896.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="150" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Robert_Louis_Stevenson_birthday_fete%2C_Samoa_1896.jpg/330px-Robert_Louis_Stevenson_birthday_fete%2C_Samoa_1896.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/d/dd/Robert_Louis_Stevenson_birthday_fete%2C_Samoa_1896.jpg/440px-Robert_Louis_Stevenson_birthday_fete%2C_Samoa_1896.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2158" data-file-height="1470"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Robert_Louis_Stevenson_birthday_fete,_Samoa_1896.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Robert_Louis_Stevenson" title="Robert Louis Stevenson">Robert Louis Stevenson</a>'s birthday fete at Vailima, 1894
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The Germans, in particular, began to show great commercial interest in the Samoan Islands, especially on the island of Upolu, where German firms monopolised <a href="/wiki/Copra" title="Copra">copra</a> and <a href="/wiki/Cocoa_bean" title="Cocoa bean">cocoa bean</a> processing. The United States laid its own claim, based on commercial shipping interests in Pearl River in <a href="/wiki/Hawaii" title="Hawaii">Hawaii</a> and Pago Pago Bay in <a href="/wiki/Eastern_Samoa" class="mw-redirect" title="Eastern Samoa">Eastern Samoa</a>, and forced alliances, most conspicuously on the islands of <a href="/wiki/Tutuila" title="Tutuila">Tutuila</a> and <a href="/wiki/Manu%27a" class="mw-redirect" title="Manu'a">Manu'a</a> which became <a href="/wiki/American_Samoa" title="American Samoa">American Samoa</a>. </p>
      <p>Britain also sent troops to protect British business enterprise, harbour rights, and consulate office. This was followed by an <a href="/wiki/Samoan_Civil_War" title="Samoan Civil War">eight-year civil war</a>, during which each of the three powers supplied arms, training and in some cases combat troops to the warring Samoan parties. The <a href="/wiki/Samoan_crisis" title="Samoan crisis">Samoan crisis</a> came to a critical juncture in March 1889 when all three colonial contenders sent warships into Apia harbour, and a larger-scale war seemed imminent. A massive storm on 15 March 1889 damaged or destroyed the warships, ending the military conflict.<sup id="cite_ref-22" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Second_Samoan_Civil_War" title="Second Samoan Civil War">Second Samoan Civil War</a> reached a head in 1898 when <a href="/wiki/German_Empire" title="German Empire">Germany</a>, the <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_of_Great_Britain_and_Ireland" title="United Kingdom of Great Britain and Ireland">United Kingdom</a>, and the United States were locked in dispute over who should control the <a href="/wiki/Samoan_Islands" title="Samoan Islands">Samoan Islands</a>. The <a href="/wiki/Siege_of_Apia" title="Siege of Apia">Siege of Apia</a> occurred in March 1899. Samoan forces loyal to Prince <a href="/wiki/Malietoa_Tanumafili_I" title="Malietoa Tanumafili I">Tanu</a> were besieged by a larger force of Samoan rebels loyal to <a href="/wiki/Mata%27afa_Iosefo" title="Mata'afa Iosefo">Mata'afa Iosefo</a>. Supporting Prince Tanu were landing parties from four British and American warships. After several days of fighting, the Samoan rebels were finally defeated.<sup id="cite_ref-23" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div class="thumb tleft">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:172px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Samoan_Paramount_chief_Mataafa_Iosefa,_1896.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Samoan_Paramount_chief_Mataafa_Iosefa%2C_1896.jpg/170px-Samoan_Paramount_chief_Mataafa_Iosefa%2C_1896.jpg" decoding="async" width="170" height="245" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Samoan_Paramount_chief_Mataafa_Iosefa%2C_1896.jpg/255px-Samoan_Paramount_chief_Mataafa_Iosefa%2C_1896.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/5/59/Samoan_Paramount_chief_Mataafa_Iosefa%2C_1896.jpg/340px-Samoan_Paramount_chief_Mataafa_Iosefa%2C_1896.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2200" data-file-height="3170"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">

         </div><a href="/wiki/Mata%27afa_Iosefo" title="Mata'afa Iosefo">Mata'afa Iosefo</a> (1832–1912) paramount chief and rival for the kingship of Samoa
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Escorting_Tanumafili_I.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Escorting_Tanumafili_I.jpg/220px-Escorting_Tanumafili_I.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="172" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Escorting_Tanumafili_I.jpg/330px-Escorting_Tanumafili_I.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/39/Escorting_Tanumafili_I.jpg/440px-Escorting_Tanumafili_I.jpg 2x" data-file-width="630" data-file-height="492"></a>

        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Lauaki_Namulau%27ulu_Mamoe_(standing_3rd_from_left_with_orator%27s_staff)_and_other_chiefs_aboard_German_warship_taking_them_to_exile_in_Saipan,_2909.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Lauaki_Namulau%27ulu_Mamoe_%28standing_3rd_from_left_with_orator%27s_staff%29_and_other_chiefs_aboard_German_warship_taking_them_to_exile_in_Saipan%2C_2909.jpg/220px-Lauaki_Namulau%27ulu_Mamoe_%28standing_3rd_from_left_with_orator%27s_staff%29_and_other_chiefs_aboard_German_warship_taking_them_to_exile_in_Saipan%2C_2909.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Lauaki_Namulau%27ulu_Mamoe_%28standing_3rd_from_left_with_orator%27s_staff%29_and_other_chiefs_aboard_German_warship_taking_them_to_exile_in_Saipan%2C_2909.jpg/330px-Lauaki_Namulau%27ulu_Mamoe_%28standing_3rd_from_left_with_orator%27s_staff%29_and_other_chiefs_aboard_German_warship_taking_them_to_exile_in_Saipan%2C_2909.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3c/Lauaki_Namulau%27ulu_Mamoe_%28standing_3rd_from_left_with_orator%27s_staff%29_and_other_chiefs_aboard_German_warship_taking_them_to_exile_in_Saipan%2C_2909.jpg/440px-Lauaki_Namulau%27ulu_Mamoe_%28standing_3rd_from_left_with_orator%27s_staff%29_and_other_chiefs_aboard_German_warship_taking_them_to_exile_in_Saipan%2C_2909.jpg 2x" data-file-width="5048" data-file-height="3968"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Lauaki_Namulau%27ulu_Mamoe_(standing_3rd_from_left_with_orator%27s_staff)_and_other_chiefs_aboard_German_warship_taking_them_to_exile_in_Saipan,_2909.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Exiled orator Lauaki Namulau'ulu Mamoe (standing 3rd from left with orator's staff) and other chiefs aboard German warship taking them to exile in Saipan, 1909
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>American and British warships shelled Apia on 15 March 1899, including the <a href="/wiki/USS_Philadelphia_(C-4)" title="USS Philadelphia (C-4)">USS <i>Philadelphia</i></a>. Germany, the United Kingdom and the United States quickly resolved to end the hostilities and divided the island chain at the <a href="/wiki/Tripartite_Convention_(1899)" class="mw-redirect" title="Tripartite Convention (1899)">Tripartite Convention of 1899</a>, signed at Washington on 2 December 1899 with ratifications exchanged on 16 February 1900.<sup id="cite_ref-GHR_24-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-GHR-24">[24]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The eastern island-group became a territory of the United States (the Tutuila Islands in 1900 and officially Manu'a in 1904) and was known as <a href="/wiki/American_Samoa" title="American Samoa">American Samoa</a>. The western islands, by far the greater landmass, became <a href="/wiki/German_Samoa" title="German Samoa">German Samoa</a>. The United Kingdom had vacated all claims in Samoa and in return received (1) termination of German rights in <a href="/wiki/Tonga" title="Tonga">Tonga</a>, (2) all of the Solomon Islands south of Bougainville, and (3) territorial alignments in West Africa.<sup id="cite_ref-25" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="German_Samoa_.281900.E2.80.931914.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="German_Samoa_(1900–1914)">German Samoa (1900–1914)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Samoa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: German Samoa (1900–1914)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Funeral_of_Tamesese.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fa/Funeral_of_Tamesese.jpg/220px-Funeral_of_Tamesese.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="175" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/thumb/f/fa/Funeral_of_Tamesese.jpg/330px-Funeral_of_Tamesese.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/en/f/fa/Funeral_of_Tamesese.jpg 2x" data-file-width="354" data-file-height="281"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Funeral_of_Tamesese.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Chiefs from all around Samoa mourning the 1929 death of Mau Movement leader, Tupua Tamesese Lealofi III, after the Black Saturday killings by NZ Soldiers.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/German_Samoa" title="German Samoa">German Samoa</a>
      </div> 
      <p>The German Empire governed the western part of the Samoan archipelago from 1900 to 1914. <a href="/wiki/Wilhelm_Solf" title="Wilhelm Solf">Wilhelm Solf</a> was appointed the colony's first governor. In 1908, when the non-violent <a href="/wiki/Mau_movement" title="Mau movement">Mau a Pule</a> resistance movement arose, Solf did not hesitate to banish the Mau leader <a href="/wiki/Lauaki_Namulauulu_Mamoe" title="Lauaki Namulauulu Mamoe">Lauaki Namulau'ulu Mamoe</a> to Saipan in the German <a href="/wiki/Northern_Mariana_Islands" title="Northern Mariana Islands">Northern Mariana Islands</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-26" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The German colonial administration governed on the principle that "there was only one government in the islands."<sup id="cite_ref-27" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup> Thus, there was no Samoan <i>Tupu</i> (king), nor an <i>alii sili</i> (similar to a governor), but two <i>Fautua</i> (advisors) were appointed by the colonial government. <i>Tumua</i> and <i>Pule</i> (traditional governments of Upolu and Savai'i) were for a time silent; all decisions on matters affecting lands and titles were under the control of the colonial Governor. </p>
      <p>In the first month of <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, on 29 August 1914, troops of the New Zealand Expeditionary Force landed unopposed on Upolu and <a href="/wiki/Occupation_of_German_Samoa" title="Occupation of German Samoa">seized control</a> from the German authorities, following a request by Great Britain for <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a> to perform this "great and urgent imperial service."<sup id="cite_ref-28" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span id="New_Zealand_rule_.281914.E2.80.931962.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="New_Zealand_rule_(1914–1962)">New Zealand rule (1914–1962)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Samoa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: New Zealand rule (1914–1962)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Western_Samoa_Trust_Territory" title="Western Samoa Trust Territory">Western Samoa Trust Territory</a>
      </div> 
      <p>From the end of <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a> until 1962, New Zealand controlled Western Samoa as a <a href="/wiki/Western_Samoa_Trust_Territory" title="Western Samoa Trust Territory">Class C Mandate</a> under <a href="/wiki/Trusteeship" class="mw-redirect" title="Trusteeship">trusteeship</a> through the <a href="/wiki/League_of_Nations" title="League of Nations">League of Nations</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-29" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> then through the United Nations. Between 1919 and 1962, Samoa was administered by the <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Island_Territories_(New_Zealand)" class="mw-redirect" title="Department of Island Territories (New Zealand)">Department of External Affairs</a>, a government department which had been specially created to oversee New Zealand's Island Territories and Samoa.<sup id="cite_ref-External_Affairs_Bill_1919_30-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-External_Affairs_Bill_1919-30">[30]</a></sup> In 1943, this Department was renamed the <a href="/wiki/Department_of_Island_Territories_(New_Zealand)" class="mw-redirect" title="Department of Island Territories (New Zealand)">Department of Island Territories</a> after a separate <a href="/wiki/Ministry_of_Foreign_Affairs_(New_Zealand)" class="mw-redirect" title="Ministry of Foreign Affairs (New Zealand)">Department of External Affairs</a> was created to conduct New Zealand's foreign affairs.<sup id="cite_ref-31" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup> During the period of New Zealand control, their administrators were responsible for two major incidents. </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Flu_pandemic">Flu pandemic</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Samoa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Flu pandemic">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>In the first incident, approximately one fifth of the Samoan population died in the <a href="/wiki/Influenza_epidemic_of_1918" class="mw-redirect" title="Influenza epidemic of 1918">influenza epidemic of 1918–1919</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-32" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 1918, during the final stages of <a href="/wiki/World_War_I" title="World War I">World War I</a>, the <a href="/wiki/Spanish_flu" title="Spanish flu">Spanish flu</a> had taken its toll, spreading rapidly from country to country. On Samoa, there had been no epidemic of pneumonic influenza in Western Samoa before the arrival of the <a href="/wiki/SS_Talune" title="SS Talune">SS <i>Talune</i></a> from <a href="/wiki/Auckland" title="Auckland">Auckland</a> on 7 November 1918. The NZ administration allowed the ship to berth in breach of quarantine; within seven days of this ship's arrival, influenza became epidemic in Upolu and then spread rapidly throughout the rest of the territory.<sup id="cite_ref-Wendt_33-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wendt-33">[33]</a></sup> Samoa suffered the most of all Pacific islands, with 90% of the population infected; 30% of adult men, 22% of adult women and 10% of children died. The cause of the epidemic was confirmed in 1919 by a Royal Commission of Inquiry into the Epidemic concluded that there had been no epidemic of pneumonic influenza in Western Samoa before the arrival of the <i>Talune</i> from Auckland on 7 November 1918.<sup id="cite_ref-Wendt_33-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Wendt-33">[33]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h4><span class="mw-headline" id="Mau_movement">Mau movement</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Samoa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Mau movement">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>The second major incident arose out of an initially peaceful protest by the <a href="/wiki/Mau_movement" title="Mau movement">Mau</a> (which literally translates as "strongly held opinion"), a non-violent popular movement which had its beginnings in the early 1900s on Savai'i, led by <a href="/wiki/Lauaki_Namulauulu_Mamoe" title="Lauaki Namulauulu Mamoe">Lauaki Namulauulu Mamoe</a>, an orator chief deposed by Solf. In 1909, Lauaki was exiled to <a href="/wiki/Saipan" title="Saipan">Saipan</a> and died en route back to Samoa in 1915. </p>
      <p>By 1918, Western Samoa had a population of some 38,000 Samoans and 1,500 Europeans.<sup id="cite_ref-34" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>However, native Samoans greatly resented New Zealand's colonial rule, and blamed inflation and the catastrophic 1918 flu epidemic on its misrule.<sup id="cite_ref-35" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> By the late 1920s the resistance movement against colonial rule had gathered widespread support. One of the Mau leaders was <a href="/wiki/Olaf_Frederick_Nelson" title="Olaf Frederick Nelson">Olaf Frederick Nelson</a>, a half Samoan and half Swedish merchant.<sup id="cite_ref-36" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> Nelson was eventually <a href="/wiki/Exile" title="Exile">exiled</a> during the late 1920s and early 1930s, but he continued to assist the organisation financially and politically. In accordance with the Mau's non-violent philosophy, the newly elected leader, High Chief Tupua Tamasese Lealofi, led his fellow uniformed Mau in a peaceful demonstration in downtown Apia on 28 December 1929.<sup id="cite_ref-37" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The New Zealand police attempted to arrest one of the leaders in the demonstration. When he resisted, a struggle developed between the police and the Mau. The officers began to fire randomly into the crowd and a <a href="/wiki/Lewis_machine_gun" class="mw-redirect" title="Lewis machine gun">Lewis machine gun</a>, mounted in preparation for this demonstration, was used to disperse the demonstrators.<sup id="cite_ref-38" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup> Mau leader and paramount chief <a href="/wiki/Tupua_Tamasese_Lealofi_III" title="Tupua Tamasese Lealofi III">Tupua Tamasese Lealofi III</a> was shot from behind and killed while trying to bring calm and order to the Mau demonstrators. Ten others died that day and approximately 50 were injured by gunshot wounds and police batons.<sup id="cite_ref-39" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-39">[39]</a></sup> That day would come to be known in Samoa as Black Saturday. The Mau grew, remaining steadfastly non-violent, and expanded to include the highly influential women's branch. </p> 
      <h4><span id="Independence_.281962.29"></span><span class="mw-headline" id="Independence_(1962)">Independence (1962)</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Samoa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Independence (1962)">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h4> 
      <p>After repeated efforts by the Samoan independence movement, the New Zealand <a href="/w/index.php?title=Western_Samoa_Act_1961&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Western Samoa Act 1961 (page does not exist)">Western Samoa Act 1961</a> of 24 November 1961 granted Samoa independence, effective on 1 January 1962, upon which the Trusteeship Agreement terminated.<sup id="cite_ref-40" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-40">[40]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-41" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup> Samoa also signed a friendship treaty with New Zealand. Samoa, the first small-island country in the Pacific to become independent, joined the <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_of_Nations" title="Commonwealth of Nations">Commonwealth of Nations</a> on 28 August 1970. While independence was achieved at the beginning of January, Samoa annually celebrates 1 June as its independence day.<sup id="cite_ref-42" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-43" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Travel writer <a href="/wiki/Paul_Theroux" title="Paul Theroux">Paul Theroux</a> noted marked differences between the societies in Western Samoa and <a href="/wiki/American_Samoa" title="American Samoa">American Samoa</a> in 1992.<sup id="cite_ref-44" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2002, New Zealand's prime minister <a href="/wiki/Helen_Clark" title="Helen Clark">Helen Clark</a> formally apologised for New Zealand's role in Spanish Influenza outbreak in 1918 that killed over a quarter of Samoa's population and for the Black Saturday killings in 1929.<sup id="cite_ref-45" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-46" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="1997_name_change">1997 name change</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Samoa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: 1997 name change">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>On 4 July 1997 the government amended the constitution to change the country's name from <i>Western Samoa</i> to <i>Samoa</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-47" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> However, in the United Nations, the country's name had always been <i>Samoa</i>.<sup id="cite_ref-U.S_Embassy_in_Samoa_48-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-U.S_Embassy_in_Samoa-48">[48]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/American_Samoa" title="American Samoa">American Samoa</a> protested against the move, asserting that the change diminished its own identity.<sup id="cite_ref-U.S_Embassy_in_Samoa_48-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-U.S_Embassy_in_Samoa-48">[48]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="21st_century">21st century</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Samoa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: 21st century">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>On 7 September 2009, the government changed the <a href="/wiki/Right-_and_left-hand_traffic" class="mw-redirect" title="Right- and left-hand traffic">rule of the road</a>, from right to left, in common with most other Commonwealth countries, most notably countries in the region such as <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>, home to large numbers of Samoans.<sup id="cite_ref-49" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> This made Samoa the first country in the 21st century to switch to driving on the left.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_50-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC-50">[50]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>At the end of December 2011, Samoa changed its time zone offset from UTC−11 to UTC+13, effectively jumping forward by one day, omitting Friday, 30 December from the local calendar. This also had the effect of changing the shape of the <a href="/wiki/International_Date_Line" title="International Date Line">International Date Line</a>, moving it to the east of the territory.<sup id="cite_ref-BBC_IDL_51-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-BBC_IDL-51">[51]</a></sup> This change aimed to help the nation boost its economy in doing business with <a href="/wiki/Australia" title="Australia">Australia</a> and <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand" title="New Zealand">New Zealand</a>. Before this change, Samoa was 21 hours behind <a href="/wiki/Sydney" title="Sydney">Sydney</a>, but the change means it is now three hours ahead. The previous time zone, implemented on 4 July 1892, operated in line with American traders based in <a href="/wiki/California" title="California">California</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-52" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-52">[52]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In 2017, Samoa signed the UN <a href="/wiki/Treaty_on_the_Prohibition_of_Nuclear_Weapons" title="Treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons">treaty on the Prohibition of Nuclear Weapons</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-53" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In June 2017, Parliament established an amendment to Article 1 of the Samoan Constitution, thereby making <a href="/wiki/Christianity" title="Christianity">Christianity</a> the state religion.<sup id="cite_ref-Religion_2-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Religion-2">[2]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-54" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In May 2021, Fiame <a href="/wiki/Naomi_Mata%CA%BBafa" title="Naomi Mataʻafa">Naomi Mataʻafa</a> is due to become Samoa's first female prime minister. Mataʻafa's <a href="/wiki/Fa%CA%BBatuatua_i_le_Atua_Samoa_ua_Tasi" title="Faʻatuatua i le Atua Samoa ua Tasi">FAST</a> party narrowly won the <a href="/wiki/2021_Samoan_general_election" class="mw-redirect" title="2021 Samoan general election">election</a>, ending the rule of long-term Prime Minister <a href="/wiki/Tuilaepa_Sailele_Malielegaoi" class="mw-redirect" title="Tuilaepa Sailele Malielegaoi">Tuilaepa Sailele Malielegaoi</a>,<sup id="cite_ref-55" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup> although the <a href="/wiki/2021_Samoan_constitutional_crisis" title="2021 Samoan constitutional crisis">constitutional crisis</a> complicates this. On 24 May 2021, she was sworn in as the new prime minister.<sup id="cite_ref-56" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-56">[56]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Government_and_politics">Government and politics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Samoa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Government and politics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Politics_of_Samoa" title="Politics of Samoa">Politics of Samoa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Fa%27amatai" class="mw-redirect" title="Fa'amatai">Fa'amatai</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Samoa_-_Apia_Govt_buildings.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Samoa_-_Apia_Govt_buildings.jpg/220px-Samoa_-_Apia_Govt_buildings.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Samoa_-_Apia_Govt_buildings.jpg/330px-Samoa_-_Apia_Govt_buildings.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b2/Samoa_-_Apia_Govt_buildings.jpg/440px-Samoa_-_Apia_Govt_buildings.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2560" data-file-height="1920"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Samoa_-_Apia_Govt_buildings.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Government buildings in <a href="/wiki/Apia" title="Apia">Apia</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Constitution_of_Samoa" title="Constitution of Samoa">1960 constitution</a>, which formally came into force with independence from New Zealand in 1962, builds on the British pattern of <a href="/wiki/Parliamentary_system" title="Parliamentary system">parliamentary democracy</a>, modified to take account of Samoan customs.<sup id="cite_ref-DS_57-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DS-57">[57]</a></sup> The national modern Government of Samoa is referred to as the <i>Malo</i>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Fiame_Mata%27afa_Faumuina_Mulinu%27u_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Fiame Mata'afa Faumuina Mulinu'u II">Fiame Mata'afa Faumuina Mulinu'u II</a>, one of the four highest-ranking <a href="/wiki/Paramount_chief" title="Paramount chief">paramount chiefs</a> in the country, became Samoa's first <a href="/wiki/Prime_Minister_of_Samoa" title="Prime Minister of Samoa">Prime Minister</a>. Two other paramount chiefs at the time of independence were appointed joint <a href="/wiki/Head_of_state" title="Head of state">heads of state</a> for life. <a href="/wiki/Tupua_Tamasese_Mea%27ole" class="mw-redirect" title="Tupua Tamasese Mea'ole">Tupua Tamasese Mea'ole</a> died in 1963, leaving <a href="/wiki/Malietoa_Tanumafili_II" title="Malietoa Tanumafili II">Malietoa Tanumafili II</a> sole head of state until his death on 11 May 2007. The next Head of State was <a href="/wiki/Tui_Atua_Tupua_Tamasese_Efi" title="Tui Atua Tupua Tamasese Efi">Tui Atua Tupua Tamasese Efi</a>, was elected by the legislature on 17 June 2007 for a fixed five-year term,<sup id="cite_ref-58" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup> and was re-elected unopposed in July 2012. He was succeeded by <a href="/wiki/Tuimalealiifano_Va%27aletoa_Sualauvi_II" title="Tuimalealiifano Va'aletoa Sualauvi II">Tuimalealiifano Va'aletoa Sualauvi II</a> in 2017. </p>
      <p>The unicameral legislature (the <a href="/wiki/Fono" class="mw-redirect" title="Fono">Fono</a>) consists of 51 members serving 5-year terms. Forty-nine are <i><a href="/wiki/Fa%27amatai" class="mw-redirect" title="Fa'amatai">matai</a></i> title-holders elected from territorial districts by Samoans; the other two are chosen by non-Samoans with no chiefly affiliation on separate electoral rolls. At least, 10% of the MPs are women.<sup id="cite_ref-59" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup> Universal suffrage was adopted in 1990, but only chiefs (matai) may stand for election to the Samoan seats. There are more than 25,000 matais in the country, about 5% of whom are women.<sup id="cite_ref-60" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup> The prime minister, chosen by a majority in the Fono, is appointed by the head of state to form a government. The prime minister's choices for the 12 <a href="/wiki/Cabinet_of_Samoa" title="Cabinet of Samoa">cabinet positions</a> are appointed by the head of state, subject to the continuing confidence of the Fono. </p>
      <p>Prominent women in Samoan politics include the late <a href="/wiki/Laulu_Fetauimalemau_Mata%27afa" class="mw-redirect" title="Laulu Fetauimalemau Mata'afa">Laulu Fetauimalemau Mata'afa</a> (1928–2007) from <a href="/wiki/Lotofaga" title="Lotofaga">Lotofaga</a> constituency, the wife of Samoa's first prime minister. Their daughter <a href="/wiki/Naomi_Mata%CA%BBafa" title="Naomi Mataʻafa">Fiame Naomi Mataʻafa</a> is a high chief and a long-serving senior member of cabinet. Other women in politics include Samoan scholar and eminent professor <a href="/wiki/Aiono_Fanaafi_Le_Tagaloa" title="Aiono Fanaafi Le Tagaloa">Aiono Fanaafi Le Tagaloa</a>, orator-chief <a href="/wiki/Matatumua_Maimoana" title="Matatumua Maimoana">Matatumua Maimoana</a> and <a href="/wiki/Safuneitu%27uga_Pa%27aga_Neri" title="Safuneitu'uga Pa'aga Neri">Safuneitu'uga Pa'aga Neri</a> (as of 2016<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Samoa&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> the Minister of Communication and Technology). </p>
      <p>The judicial system incorporates <a href="/wiki/English_common_law" class="mw-redirect" title="English common law">English common law</a> and local customs. The <a href="/wiki/Supreme_Court_of_Samoa" title="Supreme Court of Samoa">Supreme Court of Samoa</a> is the court of highest jurisdiction. The <a href="/wiki/Chief_Justice_of_Samoa" title="Chief Justice of Samoa">Chief Justice of Samoa</a> is appointed by the head of state upon the recommendation of the prime minister. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Administrative_divisions">Administrative divisions</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Samoa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Administrative divisions">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main articles: <a href="/wiki/Districts_of_Samoa" title="Districts of Samoa">Districts of Samoa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Electoral_constituencies_of_Samoa" title="Electoral constituencies of Samoa">Electoral constituencies of Samoa</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Samoa comprises eleven <i>itūmālō</i> (political districts). These are the traditional eleven districts which predate European arrival. Each district has its own constitutional foundation (<i>fa'avae</i>) based on the traditional order of title precedence found in each district's <i>faalupega</i> (traditional salutations).<sup id="cite_ref-61" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup> The capital village of each district administers and coordinates the affairs of the district and confers each district's paramount title, amongst other responsibilities. </p>
      <p>For example: </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/A%27ana" class="mw-redirect" title="A'ana">A'ana</a> has its capital at <a href="/wiki/Leulumoega" title="Leulumoega">Leulumoega</a>. The paramount <i>'tama-a-'aiga'</i> (royal lineage) title of A'ana is <a href="/wiki/Tuimaleali%27ifano" title="Tuimaleali'ifano">Tuimalealiifano</a>. The paramount <i>pāpā</i> title of A'ana is the <a href="/wiki/Tui_A%27ana_Tuimalealiifano_Va%27aletoa_Sualauvi_II" class="mw-redirect" title="Tui A'ana Tuimalealiifano Va'aletoa Sualauvi II">Tui A'ana</a>. The orator group which confers this title – the <i>Faleiva</i> (House of Nine) – is based at Leulumoega. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Atua_(district)" title="Atua (district)">Ātua</a> has its capital at <a href="/wiki/Lufilufi" title="Lufilufi">Lufilufi</a>. The paramount <i>'tama-a-'aiga'</i> (royal lineage) titles of A'ana are Tupua Tamasese (based in <a href="/wiki/Falefa" title="Falefa">Falefa</a> and Salani) and Mata'afa (based in Amaile and Lotofaga). The two main political families who confer the respective titles are <a href="/wiki/Falefa" title="Falefa">'Aiga Sā Fenunuivao</a> and '<a href="/wiki/Lotofaga" title="Lotofaga">Aiga Sā Levālasi.</a> The paramount <i>pāpā</i> title of Ātua is the <a href="/wiki/Tuiatua_Tupua_Tamasese_Efi" class="mw-redirect" title="Tuiatua Tupua Tamasese Efi">Tui Ātua</a>. The orator group which confers this title - the <i>Faleono</i> (House of Six) - is based at Lufilufi. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Tuamasaga" title="Tuamasaga">Tuamasaga</a> has its capital at <a href="/wiki/Afega" title="Afega">Afega</a>. The paramount <i>'tama-a-'aiga'</i> (royal lineage) title of Tuamasaga is the <a href="/wiki/Malietoa" title="Malietoa">Malietoa</a> title, based in <a href="/wiki/Malie" title="Malie">Malie</a>. The main political family that confers the Malietoa title is 'Aiga Sā Malietoa, with Auimatagi as the main speaker for the family. The paramount <i>pāpā</i> titles of Tuamasaga are Gatoaitele (conferred by Afega) and Vaetamasoalii (conferred by Safata).<sup id="cite_ref-:0_20-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-:0-20">[20]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The eleven <i>itūmālō</i> are identified to be: </p> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:322px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Samoa_districts_numbered2.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Samoa_districts_numbered2.png/320px-Samoa_districts_numbered2.png" decoding="async" width="320" height="156" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Samoa_districts_numbered2.png/480px-Samoa_districts_numbered2.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/2/2b/Samoa_districts_numbered2.png 2x" data-file-width="500" data-file-height="243"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Samoa_districts_numbered2.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Political districts of Samoa, including minor islands
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>On <b><a href="/wiki/Upolu" title="Upolu">Upolu</a></b> <br> </p> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        1. <a href="/wiki/Tuamasaga" title="Tuamasaga">Tuamasaga</a> (<a href="/wiki/Afega" title="Afega">Afega</a>)<sup>1</sup>
       </dd> 
       <dd>
        2. <a href="/wiki/A%27ana" class="mw-redirect" title="A'ana">A'ana</a> (<a href="/wiki/Leulumoega" title="Leulumoega">Leulumoega</a>)
       </dd> 
       <dd>
        3. <a href="/wiki/Aiga-i-le-Tai" title="Aiga-i-le-Tai">Aiga-i-le-Tai</a> (<a href="/wiki/Mulifanua" title="Mulifanua">Mulifanua</a>)<sup>2</sup>
       </dd> 
       <dd>
        4. <a href="/wiki/Atua_(district)" title="Atua (district)">Atua</a> (<a href="/wiki/Lufilufi" title="Lufilufi">Lufilufi</a>)<sup>3</sup>
       </dd> 
       <dd>
        5. <a href="/wiki/Va%27a-o-Fonoti" title="Va'a-o-Fonoti">Va'a-o-Fonoti</a> (<a href="/wiki/Samamea" title="Samamea">Samamea</a>)
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <p>On <b><a href="/wiki/Savai%27i" class="mw-redirect" title="Savai'i">Savai'i</a></b> <br> </p> 
      <dl>
       <dd>
        6. <a href="/wiki/Fa%27asaleleaga" class="mw-redirect" title="Fa'asaleleaga">Fa'asaleleaga</a> (<a href="/wiki/Safotulafai" title="Safotulafai">Safotulafai</a>)
       </dd> 
       <dd>
        7. <a href="/wiki/Gaga%27emauga" class="mw-redirect" title="Gaga'emauga">Gaga'emauga</a> (<a href="/wiki/Saleaula" title="Saleaula">Saleaula</a>)<sup>4</sup>
       </dd> 
       <dd>
        8. <a href="/wiki/Gaga%27ifomauga" class="mw-redirect" title="Gaga'ifomauga">Gaga'ifomauga</a> (<a href="/wiki/Safotu" title="Safotu">Safotu</a>)
       </dd> 
       <dd>
        9. <a href="/wiki/Vaisigano" title="Vaisigano">Vaisigano</a> (<a href="/wiki/Asau_(Samoa)" class="mw-redirect" title="Asau (Samoa)">Asau</a>)
       </dd> 
       <dd>
        10. <a href="/wiki/Satupa%27itea" class="mw-redirect" title="Satupa'itea">Satupa'itea</a> (<a href="/wiki/Satupa%27itea" class="mw-redirect" title="Satupa'itea">Satupa'itea</a>)
       </dd> 
       <dd>
        11. <a href="/wiki/Palauli" title="Palauli">Palauli</a> (<a href="/wiki/Vailoa" title="Vailoa">Vailoa</a>)
       </dd>
      </dl> 
      <p><sup>1</sup> <span style="font-size:85%;">including the faipule district of <a href="/wiki/Siumu" title="Siumu">Siumu</a></span> <br><sup>2</sup> <span style="font-size:85%;">including islands <a href="/wiki/Manono_Island" title="Manono Island">Manono</a>, <a href="/wiki/Apolima" title="Apolima">Apolima</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nu%27ulopa" class="mw-redirect" title="Nu'ulopa">Nu'ulopa</a></span> <br><sup>3</sup> <span style="font-size:85%;">including the <a href="/wiki/Aleipata_Islands" title="Aleipata Islands">Aleipata Islands</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nu%27usafe%27e" class="mw-redirect" title="Nu'usafe'e">Nu'usafe'e</a> Island</span> <br><sup>4</sup> <span style="font-size:85%;">smaller parts also on <a href="/wiki/Upolu" title="Upolu">Upolu</a> (Salamumu, incl. Salamumu-Uta and Leauvaa villages)</span> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Human_rights">Human rights</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Samoa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Human rights">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Human_rights_in_Samoa" title="Human rights in Samoa">Human rights in Samoa</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Major areas of concern include the under-representation of women, domestic violence and poor prison conditions. <a href="/wiki/LGBT_rights_in_Samoa" title="LGBT rights in Samoa">Homosexual acts</a> are illegal in Samoa.<sup id="cite_ref-62" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Christian_revival">Christian revival</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Samoa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Christian revival">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>In June 2017, an Act was passed changing the country's constitution to include a reference to the <a href="/wiki/Trinity" title="Trinity">Trinity</a>. As amended, Article 1 of the Samoan Constitution states that “Samoa is a Christian nation founded of God the Father, the Son and the Holy Spirit”. According to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Diplomat" title="The Diplomat">The Diplomat</a></i>, "What Samoa has done is shift references to Christianity into the body of the constitution, giving the text far more potential to be used in legal processes."<sup id="cite_ref-report_63-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-report-63">[63]</a></sup> The preamble to the constitution already described the country as "an independent State based on Christian principles and Samoan custom and traditions."<sup id="cite_ref-report_63-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-report-63">[63]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Geography">Geography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Samoa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Geography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Samoa_waterfall_scenery.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Samoa_waterfall_scenery.jpg/300px-Samoa_waterfall_scenery.jpg" decoding="async" width="300" height="400" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Samoa_waterfall_scenery.jpg/450px-Samoa_waterfall_scenery.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Samoa_waterfall_scenery.jpg/600px-Samoa_waterfall_scenery.jpg 2x" data-file-width="1536" data-file-height="2048"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Samoa_waterfall_scenery.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Samoa waterfall scenery
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Geography_of_Samoa" title="Geography of Samoa">Geography of Samoa</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Samoa_Country_map.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Samoa_Country_map.png/300px-Samoa_Country_map.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="154" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Samoa_Country_map.png/450px-Samoa_Country_map.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Samoa_Country_map.png/600px-Samoa_Country_map.png 2x" data-file-width="800" data-file-height="411"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Samoa_Country_map.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A map of Samoa.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:302px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Samoa_topography.png" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Samoa_topography.png/300px-Samoa_topography.png" decoding="async" width="300" height="161" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Samoa_topography.png/450px-Samoa_topography.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/ce/Samoa_topography.png/600px-Samoa_topography.png 2x" data-file-width="2000" data-file-height="1074"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Samoa_topography.png" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Topography of Samoa.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>Samoa lies south of the equator, about halfway between Hawaii and New Zealand, in the <a href="/wiki/Polynesia" title="Polynesia">Polynesian</a> region of the Pacific Ocean. The total land area is 2,842&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (1,097&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi),<sup id="cite_ref-64" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup> consisting of the two large islands of <a href="/wiki/Upolu" title="Upolu">Upolu</a> and <a href="/wiki/Savai%27i" class="mw-redirect" title="Savai'i">Savai'i</a> (which together account for 99% of the total land area) and eight small islets. </p>
      <p>The islets are:<sup id="cite_ref-DB_65-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DB-65">[65]</a></sup> </p> 
      <ul>
       <li>the three islets in the <a href="/wiki/Apolima_Strait" title="Apolima Strait">Apolima Strait</a> (<a href="/wiki/Manono_Island" title="Manono Island">Manono Island</a>, <a href="/wiki/Apolima" title="Apolima">Apolima</a> and <a href="/wiki/Nu%27ulopa" class="mw-redirect" title="Nu'ulopa">Nu'ulopa</a>)</li> 
       <li>the four <a href="/wiki/Aleipata_Islands" title="Aleipata Islands">Aleipata Islands</a> off the eastern end of Upolu (<a href="/wiki/Nu%27utele" class="mw-redirect" title="Nu'utele">Nu'utele</a>, <a href="/wiki/Nu%27ulua" class="mw-redirect" title="Nu'ulua">Nu'ulua</a>, <a href="/wiki/Namua" title="Namua">Namua</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Fanuatapu" title="Fanuatapu">Fanuatapu</a>)</li> 
       <li><a href="/wiki/Nu%27usafe%27e" class="mw-redirect" title="Nu'usafe'e">Nu'usafe'e</a>, which is less than 1 hectare (2½ acres) in area and lies about 1.4&nbsp;km (0.9&nbsp;mi) off the south coast of Upolu at the village of <i>Vaovai</i></li>
      </ul> 
      <p>The main island of Upolu is home to nearly three-quarters of Samoa's population, and to the capital city, <a href="/wiki/Apia,_Samoa" class="mw-redirect" title="Apia, Samoa">Apia</a>. </p>
      <p>The Samoan islands result geologically from <a href="/wiki/Volcanism" title="Volcanism">volcanism</a>, originating with the <a href="/wiki/Samoa_hotspot" title="Samoa hotspot">Samoa hotspot</a>, which probably results from a <a href="/wiki/Mantle_plume" title="Mantle plume">mantle plume</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-66" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-67" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup> While all of the islands have volcanic origins, only Savai'i, the westernmost island in Samoa, remains volcanically active, with the most recent eruptions at <a href="/wiki/Mt_Matavanu" class="mw-redirect" title="Mt Matavanu">Mt Matavanu</a> (1905–1911), <a href="/wiki/Mata_Ole_Afi" class="mw-redirect" title="Mata Ole Afi">Mata o le Afi</a> (1902) and <a href="/wiki/Mauga_Afi" title="Mauga Afi">Mauga Afi</a> (1725). The highest point in Samoa is <a href="/wiki/Silisili" title="Silisili">Mt Silisili</a>, at 1858&nbsp;m (6,096&nbsp;ft). The <a href="/wiki/Saleaula" title="Saleaula">Saleaula</a> lava fields situated on the central north coast of Savai'i result from the Mt Matavanu eruptions, which left 50&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (20&nbsp;sq&nbsp;mi) of solidified lava.<sup id="cite_ref-68" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Savai'i is the largest of the Samoan islands and the sixth-largest Polynesian island (after New Zealand's <a href="/wiki/North_Island" title="North Island">North</a>, <a href="/wiki/South_Island" title="South Island">South</a> and <a href="/wiki/Stewart_Island/Rakiura" class="mw-redirect" title="Stewart Island/Rakiura">Stewart Islands</a> and the Hawaiian islands of <a href="/wiki/Hawaii_(island)" title="Hawaii (island)">Hawaiʻi</a> and <a href="/wiki/Maui" title="Maui">Maui</a>). The population of Savai'i is 42,000 people. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Climate">Climate</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Samoa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Climate">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>Samoa has an equatorial climate, with an average annual temperature of 26.5&nbsp;°C (79.7&nbsp;°F) and a main rainy season from November to April, although heavy rain may fall in any month.<sup id="cite_ref-69" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup> </p> 
      <div style="clear:both;"></div>
