      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ecology">Ecology</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Samoa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Ecology">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/List_of_mammals_of_Samoa" title="List of mammals of Samoa">List of mammals of Samoa</a> and <a href="/wiki/Samoan_plant_names" class="mw-redirect" title="Samoan plant names">Samoan plant names</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/List_of_birds_of_Samoa" title="List of birds of Samoa">List of birds of Samoa</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_protected_areas_of_Samoa" title="List of protected areas of Samoa">List of protected areas of Samoa</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Samoa forms part of the <a href="/wiki/Samoan_tropical_moist_forests" title="Samoan tropical moist forests">Samoan tropical moist forests</a> ecoregion.<sup id="cite_ref-DinersteinOlson2017_71-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DinersteinOlson2017-71">[71]</a></sup> Since human habitation began, about 80% of the lowland rainforests have disappeared. Within the ecoregion about 28% of plants and 84% of land birds are endemic.<sup id="cite_ref-72" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Economy">Economy</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Samoa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Economy">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Economy_of_Samoa" title="Economy of Samoa">Economy of Samoa</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Central_Bank_of_Samoa_(2009).jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Central_Bank_of_Samoa_%282009%29.jpg/220px-Central_Bank_of_Samoa_%282009%29.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Central_Bank_of_Samoa_%282009%29.jpg/330px-Central_Bank_of_Samoa_%282009%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/8/8e/Central_Bank_of_Samoa_%282009%29.jpg/440px-Central_Bank_of_Samoa_%282009%29.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2272" data-file-height="1704"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Central_Bank_of_Samoa_(2009).jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_Samoa" title="Central Bank of Samoa">Central Bank of Samoa</a>
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Samoa_electricity_production.svg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Samoa_electricity_production.svg/220px-Samoa_electricity_production.svg.png" decoding="async" width="220" height="201" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Samoa_electricity_production.svg/330px-Samoa_electricity_production.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/2b/Samoa_electricity_production.svg/440px-Samoa_electricity_production.svg.png 2x" data-file-width="639" data-file-height="585"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Samoa_electricity_production.svg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Samoa electricity production by source
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Colocasia_esculenta_dsc07801.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Colocasia_esculenta_dsc07801.jpg/220px-Colocasia_esculenta_dsc07801.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Colocasia_esculenta_dsc07801.jpg/330px-Colocasia_esculenta_dsc07801.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/c/c2/Colocasia_esculenta_dsc07801.jpg/440px-Colocasia_esculenta_dsc07801.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2592" data-file-height="1944"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Colocasia_esculenta_dsc07801.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div><a href="/wiki/Taro" title="Taro">Taro</a>, a root crop, traditionally was Samoa's largest export, generating more than half of all export revenue in 1993. A fungal blight decimated the plants, and in each year since 1994 taro exports have accounted for less than 1% of export revenue.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/United_Nations" title="United Nations">United Nations</a> has classified Samoa as an <a href="/wiki/Developing_country" title="Developing country"> economically developing country</a> since 2014.<sup id="cite_ref-73" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup> As of 2017<sup class="plainlinks noexcerpt noprint asof-tag update" style="display:none;"><a class="external text" href="https://en.wikipedia.org/w/index.php?title=Samoa&amp;action=edit">[update]</a></sup> Samoa's gross domestic product in <a href="/wiki/Purchasing-power_parity" class="mw-redirect" title="Purchasing-power parity">purchasing-power parity</a> was estimated<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (May 2021)">by whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> at $1.13 billion <a href="/wiki/United_States_dollar" title="United States dollar">U.S. dollars</a>, ranking the country 204th in the world. The <a href="/wiki/Tertiary_sector_of_the_economy" title="Tertiary sector of the economy">services sector</a> accounted for 66% of GDP, followed by <a href="/wiki/Industrial_sector" class="mw-redirect" title="Industrial sector"> industry</a> and <a href="/wiki/Agriculture" title="Agriculture">agriculture</a> at 23.6% and 10.4% respectively.<sup id="cite_ref-CIASamoa_74-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIASamoa-74">[74]</a></sup> For the same year, the Samoan <a href="/wiki/Workforce" title="Workforce">labour force</a> was estimated<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Words_to_watch#Unsupported_attributions" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Words to watch"><span title="The material near this tag may use weasel words or too-vague attribution. (May 2021)">by whom?</span></a></i>]</sup> at 50,700.<sup id="cite_ref-CIASamoa_74-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-CIASamoa-74">[74]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Central_Bank_of_Samoa" title="Central Bank of Samoa">Central Bank of Samoa</a> issues and regulates Samoa's currency, the <a href="/wiki/Samoan_tala" class="mw-redirect" title="Samoan tala"> Samoan tālā</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-75" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-75">[75]</a></sup> The economy of Samoa has traditionally depended on agriculture and fishing at the local level. In modern times, <a href="/wiki/Development_aid" title="Development aid">development aid</a>, private family <a href="/wiki/Remittances_from_overseas" class="mw-redirect" title="Remittances from overseas">remittances from overseas</a>, and agricultural exports have become key factors in the nation's economy. Agriculture employs two-thirds of the labour force and furnishes 90% of exports, featuring <a href="/wiki/Coconut" title="Coconut">coconut</a> cream, <a href="/wiki/Coconut_oil" title="Coconut oil">coconut oil</a>, <a href="/wiki/Noni" class="mw-redirect" title="Noni">noni</a> (juice of the <i>nonu</i> fruit, as it is known in Samoan), and <a href="/wiki/Copra" title="Copra">copra</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-cia_1-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-1">[1]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Outside of a large automotive <a href="/wiki/Wire_harness" class="mw-redirect" title="Wire harness">wire harness</a> factory (<a href="/wiki/Yazaki" title="Yazaki">Yazaki Corporation</a> which ended production in August 2017<sup id="cite_ref-76" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup>), the manufacturing sector mainly processes agricultural products. Prior to the <a href="/wiki/COVID-19_pandemic_in_Samoa" title="COVID-19 pandemic in Samoa"> COVID-19 pandemic</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tourism_in_Samoa" class="mw-redirect" title="Tourism in Samoa"> tourism</a> expanded, accounting for 25% of GDP.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (May 2021)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> Tourist arrivals increased over the years with more than 100,000 tourists visiting the islands in 2005, up from 70,000 in 1996. </p>
      <p>The Samoan government has called for <a href="/wiki/Deregulation" title="Deregulation">deregulation</a> of the financial sector, encouragement of investment, and continued fiscal discipline.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Observers point to the flexibility of the labour market as a basic strength for future economic advances.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> The sector<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Avoid_weasel_words" class="mw-redirect" title="Wikipedia:Avoid weasel words"><span title="The material near this tag possibly uses too vague attribution or weasel words. (May 2021)">which?</span></a></i>]</sup> has been helped enormously by major capital investment in hotel infrastructure, political instability in neighbouring Pacific countries, and the 2005 launch of <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Samoa" title="Virgin Samoa">Virgin Samoa</a> a joint-venture between the government and <a href="/wiki/Virgin_Australia" title="Virgin Australia">Virgin Australia</a> (then Virgin Blue). </p>
      <p>In the period before German colonisation (from the late 19th century), Samoa produced mostly copra. German merchants and settlers were active in introducing large-scale <a href="/wiki/Plantation" title="Plantation">plantation</a> operations and in developing new industries, notably cocoa beans and rubber, relying on imported labourers from China and <a href="/wiki/Melanesia" title="Melanesia">Melanesia</a>. When the value of <a href="/wiki/Natural_rubber" title="Natural rubber">natural rubber</a> fell drastically, about the end of the Great War (World War I) in 1918, the New Zealand government encouraged the production of bananas, for which there is a large market in New Zealand.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (October 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Because of variations in altitude, Samoa can cultivate a large range of tropical and subtropical crops. Land is not generally available to outside interests. Of the total land area of 2,934&nbsp;km<sup>2</sup> (725,000 acres), about 24.4% is in permanent crops and another 21.2% is arable. About 4.4% is Western Samoan Trust Estates Corporation (WSTEC).<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2008)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The staple products of Samoa are copra (dried coconut meat), <a href="/wiki/Cocoa_bean" title="Cocoa bean">cocoa beans</a> (for chocolate), rubber, and bananas.<sup id="cite_ref-77" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> The annual production of both bananas and copra has been<sup class="noprint Inline-Template" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Manual_of_Style/Dates_and_numbers#Chronological_items" title="Wikipedia:Manual of Style/Dates and numbers"><span title="The time period mentioned near this tag is ambiguous. (May 2021)">when?</span></a></i>]</sup> in the range of 13,000 to 15,000 metric tons (about 14,500 to 16,500 short tons). If the <a href="/wiki/Asiatic_rhinoceros_beetle" title="Asiatic rhinoceros beetle">Asiatic rhinoceros beetle</a> in Samoa were eradicated, Samoa could produce in excess of 40,000 metric tons (44,000 short tons) of copra. Samoan cocoa beans are of very high quality and are used in fine New Zealand chocolates. Most are <a href="/wiki/Criollo_(cocoa_bean)" class="mw-redirect" title="Criollo (cocoa bean)"> Criollo</a>-Forastero hybrids. Coffee grows well, but production has been uneven. WSTEC is the biggest coffee producer. </p>
      <p>Other agricultural industries have proven less successful. <a href="/wiki/Sugarcane" title="Sugarcane">Sugarcane</a> production, originally established by Germans in the early 20th century, could be successful.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (May 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> Old train tracks for transporting cane can be seen at some plantations east of <a href="/wiki/Apia" title="Apia">Apia</a>. <a href="/wiki/Pineapple" title="Pineapple">Pineapples</a> grow well in Samoa, but have not moved beyond local consumption to become a major export.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Sixty percent of Samoa's electricity comes from renewable <a href="/wiki/Hydroelectricity" title="Hydroelectricity"> hydro</a>, solar, and wind sources, with the remainder produced by diesel generators. The Electric Power Corporation set a goal of <a href="/wiki/100%25_renewable_energy" title="100% renewable energy">100% renewable energy</a> by 2021.<sup id="cite_ref-78" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-78">[78]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Demographics">Demographics</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Samoa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Demographics">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Samoa_Familie.JPG" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Samoa_Familie.JPG/220px-Samoa_Familie.JPG" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Samoa_Familie.JPG/330px-Samoa_Familie.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/fc/Samoa_Familie.JPG/440px-Samoa_Familie.JPG 2x" data-file-width="2048" data-file-height="1536"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Samoa_Familie.JPG" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A Samoan family
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Demographics_of_Samoa" title="Demographics of Samoa">Demographics of Samoa</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Samoa reported a population of 194,320 in its 2016 census.<sup id="cite_ref-census_3-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-census-3">[3]</a></sup> About three-quarters of the population live on the main island of <a href="/wiki/Upolu" title="Upolu">Upolu</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-DS_57-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DS-57">[57]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Health">Health</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Samoa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Health">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/2019_Samoa_measles_outbreak" title="2019 Samoa measles outbreak">2019 Samoa measles outbreak</a>
      </div> 
      <p>A measles outbreak began in October 2019 and is currently ongoing. As of 7 December, there have been 68 deaths (0.31 per 1,000, based on a population of 201,316<sup id="cite_ref-79" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup>) and over 4,460 cases (2.2% of the population) of measles in Samoa,<sup id="cite_ref-DeathToll_80-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-DeathToll-80">[80]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-81" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup> mainly children under four years old, and 10 reported cases in <a href="/wiki/Fiji" title="Fiji">Fiji</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-82" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> It is expected that 70 people will die and up to 6,500 people will be infected.<sup id="cite_ref-83" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ethnic_groups">Ethnic groups</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Samoa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Ethnic groups">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p>The population is 92.6% <a href="/wiki/Samoans" title="Samoans">Samoans</a>, 7% <a href="/wiki/Euronesian" title="Euronesian">Euronesian</a> (people of mixed <a href="/wiki/Europeans" class="mw-redirect" title="Europeans">European</a> and <a href="/wiki/Polynesians" title="Polynesians">Polynesian</a> ancestry) and 0.4% Europeans, according to the <a href="/wiki/The_World_Factbook" title="The World Factbook">CIA World Factbook</a>. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Languages">Languages</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Samoa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Languages">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Polynesian_languages" title="Polynesian languages">Polynesian languages</a>
      </div> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Samoan_language" title="Samoan language">Samoan</a> (<i>Gagana Fa'asāmoa</i>) and <a href="/wiki/English_language" title="English language">English</a> are the official languages. Including second-language speakers, there are more speakers of Samoan than English in Samoa.<sup id="cite_ref-84" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Samoan_Sign_Language" title="Samoan Sign Language">Samoan Sign Language</a> is also commonly used among the <a href="/wiki/Hearing_loss" title="Hearing loss">deaf</a> population of Samoa. To emphasize the importance of full inclusion with sign language, elementary Samoan Sign Language was taught to members of the Samoa Police Service, Red Cross Society, and public during the 2017 International Week of the Deaf.<sup id="cite_ref-85" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-85">[85]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Religion">Religion</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Samoa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Religion">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Further information: <a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Samoa" title="Religion in Samoa">Religion in Samoa</a>
      </div> 
      <p>Since 2017, Article 1 of the Samoan Constitution states that “Samoa is a Christian nation founded of God the Father, the Son and the Holy Spirit”.<sup id="cite_ref-Religion_2-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Religion-2">[2]</a></sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Religion_in_Samoa" title="Religion in Samoa">Samoans' religious adherence</a> includes the following: <a href="/wiki/Christian_Congregational_Church_of_Samoa" title="Christian Congregational Church of Samoa">Christian Congregational Church of Samoa</a> 31.8%, <a href="/wiki/Roman_Catholic_Church" class="mw-redirect" title="Roman Catholic Church">Roman Catholic</a> 19.4%, <a href="/wiki/Methodist" class="mw-redirect" title="Methodist">Methodist</a> 15.2%, <a href="/wiki/Samoan_Assemblies_of_God" title="Samoan Assemblies of God">Assembly of God</a> 13.7%, <a href="/wiki/The_Church_of_Jesus_Christ_of_Latter-day_Saints_in_Samoa" class="mw-redirect" title="The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints in Samoa">The Church of Jesus Christ of Latter-day Saints</a> 7.6%, <a href="/wiki/Seventh-day_Adventist_Church" title="Seventh-day Adventist Church">Seventh-day Adventist</a> 3.9%, Worship Centre 1.7%, other Christian 5.5%, other 0.7%, none 0.1%, unspecified 0.1% (2011 estimate).<sup id="cite_ref-cia_1-2" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-cia-1">[1]</a></sup> The Head of State until 2007, <a href="/wiki/Malietoa_Tanumafili_II_of_Samoa" class="mw-redirect" title="Malietoa Tanumafili II of Samoa">Malietoa Tanumafili II</a>, was a <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_Faith" title="Baháʼí Faith">Baháʼí</a>. Samoa hosts the seventh (of nine current) <a href="/wiki/Bah%C3%A1%CA%BC%C3%AD_House_of_Worship" title="Baháʼí House of Worship">Baháʼí Houses of Worship</a> in the world; completed in 1984 and dedicated by the Head of State, it is located in <a href="/w/index.php?title=Tiapapata&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Tiapapata (page does not exist)">Tiapapata</a>, 8&nbsp;km (5&nbsp;mi) from <a href="/wiki/Apia" title="Apia">Apia</a>. </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Education">Education</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Samoa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: Education">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <p>The Samoan government provides eight years of primary and secondary education that is tuition-free and is compulsory through age 16.<sup id="cite_ref-86" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-86">[86]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>In Samoa primary education is free, which includes grades 1–8, Ages 6–13, and is a total of 6 years. After primary education comes middle school which is also free and is only 2 years. After 8 years students are required to take a national exam which ranks them for selection into secondary schools. Once the students are in secondary school everything is taught to them in English and they also have to pay yearly tuition, which is $60 for Samoan citizens and $150 for non Samoan citizen students. </p>
      <p>Samoa's main post-secondary educational institution is the <a href="/wiki/National_University_of_Samoa" title="National University of Samoa">National University of Samoa</a>, established in 1984. The country is also home to several branches of the multi-national <a href="/wiki/University_of_the_South_Pacific" title="University of the South Pacific">University of the South Pacific</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Oceania_University_of_Medicine" title="Oceania University of Medicine">Oceania University of Medicine</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-87" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-87">[87]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Education in Samoa has proved to be effective as a 2012 <a href="/wiki/UNESCO" title="UNESCO">UNESCO</a> report stated that 99 per cent of Samoan adults are literate.<sup id="cite_ref-88" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-88">[88]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Culture">Culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Samoa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: Culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       Main article: <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Samoa" class="mw-redirect" title="Culture of Samoa">Culture of Samoa</a>
      </div> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Music_of_Samoa" title="Music of Samoa">Music of Samoa</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:262px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Samoa_upolu.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Samoa_upolu.jpg/260px-Samoa_upolu.jpg" decoding="async" width="260" height="173" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Samoa_upolu.jpg/390px-Samoa_upolu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/6/69/Samoa_upolu.jpg/520px-Samoa_upolu.jpg 2x" data-file-width="886" data-file-height="591"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Samoa_upolu.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A view of <a href="/wiki/Falefa_Valley" title="Falefa Valley">Falefa Valley</a> from Le Mafa Pass, east <a href="/wiki/Upolu" title="Upolu">Upolu</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The <a href="/wiki/Fa%27a_Samoa" class="mw-redirect" title="Fa'a Samoa">fa'a Samoa</a>, or traditional Samoan way, remains a strong force in Samoan life and politics. As one of the oldest Polynesian cultures, the fa'asamoa developed over a period of 3,000 years, withstanding centuries of European influence to maintain its historical customs, social and political systems, and <a href="/wiki/Samoan_language" title="Samoan language">language</a>. Cultural customs such as the <a href="/wiki/Samoa_%27ava_ceremony" class="mw-redirect" title="Samoa 'ava ceremony">Samoa 'ava ceremony</a> are significant and solemn rituals at important occasions including the bestowal of <i><a href="/wiki/Fa%27amatai" class="mw-redirect" title="Fa'amatai">matai</a></i> chiefly titles. Items of great cultural value include the finely woven <i><a href="/wiki/%27ie_toga" class="mw-redirect" title="'ie toga">'ie toga</a></i>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Samoan_mythology" title="Samoan mythology">Samoan mythology</a> includes many gods with creation stories and figures of legend such as <a href="/wiki/Tagaloa" title="Tagaloa">Tagaloa</a> and the goddess of war <a href="/wiki/Nafanua" title="Nafanua">Nafanua</a>, the daughter of <a href="/wiki/Saveasi%27uleo" class="mw-redirect" title="Saveasi'uleo">Saveasi'uleo</a>, ruler of the spirit realm <a href="/wiki/Pulotu" title="Pulotu">Pulotu</a>. Other legends include the well known story of <a href="/wiki/Sina_and_the_Eel" title="Sina and the Eel">Sina and the Eel</a> which explains the origins of the first coconut tree. </p>
      <p>Some Samoans are spiritual and religious, and have subtly adapted the dominant religion of Christianity to 'fit in' with fa'a Samoa and vice versa. Ancient beliefs continue to co-exist side by side with Christianity, particularly in regard to the traditional customs and rituals of fa'a Samoa. The Samoan culture is centred around the principle of vāfealoa'i, the relationships between people. These relationships are based on respect, or <a href="/w/index.php?title=Fa%27aaloalo&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" class="new" title="Fa'aaloalo (page does not exist)">fa'aaloalo</a>. When Christianity was introduced in Samoa, most Samoan people converted. Currently 98% of the population identify themselves as Christian.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (March 2021)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>Some Samoans live a communal way of life, participating in activities collectively. Examples of this are the traditional Samoan <i><a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Samoa" title="Architecture of Samoa">fale</a></i> (houses) which are open with no walls, using blinds made of coconut palm fronds during the night or bad weather. </p>
      <p>The Samoan <i><a href="/wiki/Siva_Samoa" title="Siva Samoa">siva</a></i> dance has unique gentle movements of the body in time to music and tells a story, although the Samoan male dances can be more snappy.<sup id="cite_ref-89" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-89">[89]</a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/Sasa_(dance)" title="Sasa (dance)">sasa</a></i> is also a traditional dance where rows of dancers perform rapid <a href="/wiki/Synchronization" title="Synchronization">synchronised</a> movements in time to the rhythm of wooden drums <i>(<a href="/wiki/Pate_(musical_instrument)" class="mw-redirect" title="Pate (musical instrument)">pate</a>)</i> or rolled mats. Another dance performed by males is called the <i><a href="/wiki/Fa%27ataupati" title="Fa'ataupati">fa'ataupati</a></i> or the slap dance, creating rhythmic sounds by slapping different parts of the body. This is believed to have been derived from slapping insects on the body.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (November 2017)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> </p>
      <p>The form and construction of traditional <a href="/wiki/Architecture_of_Samoa" title="Architecture of Samoa">architecture of Samoa</a> was a specialised skill by <i>Tufuga fai fale</i> that was also linked to other cultural artforms. </p> 
      <ul class="gallery mw-gallery-packed">

        </div></li> 
      </ul> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Tattooing">Tattooing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Samoa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=26" title="Edit section: Tattooing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Samoan_Malu.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Samoan_Malu.jpg/220px-Samoan_Malu.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="165" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Samoan_Malu.jpg/330px-Samoan_Malu.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/f/f1/Samoan_Malu.jpg/440px-Samoan_Malu.jpg 2x" data-file-width="2304" data-file-height="1728"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Samoan_Malu.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>A Samoan woman with a traditional <a href="/wiki/Malu" title="Malu">malu</a>.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>As with other Polynesian cultures (<a href="/wiki/Hawaiian_culture" class="mw-redirect" title="Hawaiian culture">Hawaiian</a>, <a href="/wiki/Tahitians" title="Tahitians">Tahitian</a> and <a href="/wiki/M%C4%81ori_culture" title="Māori culture">Māori</a>) with significant and unique tattoos, Samoans have two gender specific and culturally significant tattoos. For males, it is called the <a href="/wiki/Pe%27a" title="Pe'a">Pe'a</a> and consists of intricate and geometrical patterns <a href="/wiki/Tattoo" title="Tattoo">tattooed</a> that cover areas from the knees up towards the ribs. A male who possesses such a tatau is called a <a href="/wiki/Soga%27imiti" class="mw-redirect" title="Soga'imiti">soga'imiti</a>. A Samoan girl or <i>teine</i> is given a <a href="/wiki/Malu" title="Malu">malu</a>, which covers the area from just below her knees to her upper thighs.<sup id="cite_ref-90" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-90">[90]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Contemporary_culture">Contemporary culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Samoa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=27" title="Edit section: Contemporary culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <p><a href="/wiki/Albert_Wendt" title="Albert Wendt">Albert Wendt</a> is a significant Samoan writer whose novels and stories tell the Samoan experience. In 1989, his novel <i>Flying Fox in a Freedom Tree</i> was made into a feature film in New Zealand, directed by Martyn Sanderson.<sup id="cite_ref-91" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-91">[91]</a></sup> Another novel <i>Sons for the Return Home</i> had also been made into a feature film in 1979, directed by Paul Maunder.<sup id="cite_ref-92" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-92">[92]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The late <a href="/wiki/John_Kneubuhl" title="John Kneubuhl">John Kneubuhl</a>, born in American Samoa, was an accomplished playwright and screenwriter and writer. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Sia_Figiel" title="Sia Figiel">Sia Figiel</a> won the 1997 <a href="/wiki/Commonwealth_Writers%27_Prize" class="mw-redirect" title="Commonwealth Writers' Prize">Commonwealth Writers' Prize</a> for fiction in the south-east Asia/South Pacific region with her novel "Where We Once Belonged". </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Momoe_Malietoa_Von_Reiche" title="Momoe Malietoa Von Reiche">Momoe Malietoa Von Reiche</a> is an internationally recognised poet and artist. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Tusiata_Avia" title="Tusiata Avia">Tusiata Avia</a> is a performance poet. Her first book of poetry <i>Wild Dogs Under My Skirt</i> was published by Victoria University Press in 2004. <a href="/wiki/Dan_Taulapapa_McMullin" title="Dan Taulapapa McMullin">Dan Taulapapa McMullin</a> is an artist and writer. </p>
      <p>Other Samoan poets and writers include <a href="/wiki/Sapa%27u_Ruperake_Petaia" title="Sapa'u Ruperake Petaia">Sapa'u Ruperake Petaia</a>, <a href="/wiki/Eti_Sa%27aga" class="mw-redirect" title="Eti Sa'aga">Eti Sa'aga</a> and <a href="/wiki/Savea_Sano_Malifa" title="Savea Sano Malifa">Savea Sano Malifa</a>, the editor of the <a href="/wiki/Samoa_Observer" title="Samoa Observer">Samoa Observer</a>. </p>
      <p>In music, popular local bands include <a href="/wiki/The_Five_Stars" title="The Five Stars">The Five Stars</a>, Penina o Tiafau and Punialava'a. <a href="/wiki/The_Yandall_Sisters" title="The Yandall Sisters">The Yandall Sisters</a>' cover of the song <i>Sweet Inspiration</i> reached number one on the New Zealand charts in 1974. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/King_Kapisi" title="King Kapisi">King Kapisi</a> was the first hip hop artist to receive the prestigious New Zealand <a href="/wiki/Australasian_Performing_Right_Association" class="mw-redirect" title="Australasian Performing Right Association">APRA</a> Silver Scroll Award in 1999 for his song <i>Reverse Resistance</i>. The music video for <i>Reverse Resistance</i> was filmed in Savai'i at his villages. </p>
      <p>Other successful Samoan hip hop artists include rapper <a href="/wiki/Scribe_(rapper)" title="Scribe (rapper)">Scribe</a>, <a href="/wiki/Dei_Hamo" title="Dei Hamo">Dei Hamo</a>, <a href="/wiki/Savage_(rapper)" title="Savage (rapper)">Savage</a> and <a href="/wiki/Tha_Feelstyle" title="Tha Feelstyle">Tha Feelstyle</a> whose music video <i>Suamalie</i> was filmed in Samoa. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Lemi_Ponifasio" title="Lemi Ponifasio">Lemi Ponifasio</a> is a director and choreographer who is prominent internationally with his dance Company MAU.<sup id="cite_ref-93" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-93">[93]</a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Neil_Ieremia" title="Neil Ieremia">Neil Ieremia</a>'s company <a href="/wiki/Black_Grace" title="Black Grace">Black Grace</a> has also received international acclaim with tours to Europe and New York. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Hip_hop" title="Hip hop">Hip hop</a> has had a significant impact on Samoan culture. According to Katerina Martina Teaiwa, PhD from the University of Hawaii at Manoa, "Hip hop culture in particular is popular amongst Samoan youth."<sup id="cite_ref-Dances_94-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dances-94">[94]</a></sup> As in many other countries, hip hop music is popular. In addition, the integration of hip hop elements into Samoan tradition also "testifies to the transferability of the dance forms themselves," and to the "circuits through which people and all their embodied knowledge travel."<sup id="cite_ref-95" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-95">[95]</a></sup> Dance both in its traditional form and its more modern forms has remained a central cultural currency to Samoans, especially youths.<sup id="cite_ref-Dances_94-1" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Dances-94">[94]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>The arts organisation <i>Tautai</i> is a collective of visual artists including <a href="/wiki/Fatu_Feu%27u" title="Fatu Feu'u">Fatu Feu'u</a>, <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Penisula" title="Johnny Penisula">Johnny Penisula</a>, <a href="/wiki/Shigeyuki_Kihara" class="mw-redirect" title="Shigeyuki Kihara">Shigeyuki Kihara</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michel_Tuffery" title="Michel Tuffery">Michel Tuffery</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Lily_Laita" title="Lily Laita">Lily Laita</a>.<sup id="cite_ref-96" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-96">[96]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Director <a href="/wiki/Sima_Urale" title="Sima Urale">Sima Urale</a> is a filmmaker. Urale's short film <i>O Tamaiti</i> won the prestigious Best Short Film at the <a href="/wiki/Venice_Film_Festival" title="Venice Film Festival">Venice Film Festival</a> in 1996. Her first feature film <i>Apron Strings</i> opened the 2008 <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_International_Film_Festivals" class="mw-redirect" title="New Zealand International Film Festivals">NZ International Film Festival</a>. The feature film <i><a href="/wiki/Siones_Wedding" class="mw-redirect" title="Siones Wedding">Siones Wedding</a></i>, co-written by <a href="/wiki/Oscar_Kightley" title="Oscar Kightley">Oscar Kightley</a>, was financially successful following premieres in Auckland and Apia. The 2011 film <a href="/wiki/The_Orator_(film)" title="The Orator (film)">The Orator</a> was the first ever fully Samoan film, shot in Samoa in the Samoan language with a Samoan cast telling a uniquely Samoan story. Written and directed by <a href="/wiki/Tusi_Tamasese" title="Tusi Tamasese">Tusi Tamasese</a>, it received much critical acclaim and attention at film festivals throughout the world. </p> 
      <h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Sport">Sport</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Samoa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Sport">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3> 
      <div role="note" class="hatnote navigation-not-searchable">
       See also: <a href="/wiki/Sport_in_Samoa" title="Sport in Samoa">Sport in Samoa</a>
      </div> 
      <div class="thumb tright">
       <div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;">
        <a href="/wiki/File:Percy_Montgomery_against_Samoa.jpg" class="image"><img alt="" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Percy_Montgomery_against_Samoa.jpg/220px-Percy_Montgomery_against_Samoa.jpg" decoding="async" width="220" height="147" class="thumbimage" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Percy_Montgomery_against_Samoa.jpg/330px-Percy_Montgomery_against_Samoa.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Percy_Montgomery_against_Samoa.jpg/440px-Percy_Montgomery_against_Samoa.jpg 2x" data-file-width="591" data-file-height="396"></a> 
        <div class="thumbcaption">
         <div class="magnify">
          <a href="/wiki/File:Percy_Montgomery_against_Samoa.jpg" class="internal" title="Enlarge"></a>
         </div>Samoa (blue) vs. South Africa in June 2007.
        </div>
       </div>
      </div> 
      <p>The main sports played in Samoa are <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a>, <a href="/wiki/Samoan_cricket" class="mw-redirect" title="Samoan cricket">Samoan cricket</a> and <a href="/wiki/Netball" title="Netball">netball</a>. Rugby union is the national football code of Samoa. In Samoan villages, volleyball is also popular. </p>
      <p>Rugby union is the national sport in Samoa and the <a href="/wiki/Samoa_national_rugby_union_team" title="Samoa national rugby union team">national team</a>, nicknamed the Manu Samoa, is consistently competitive against teams from vastly more populous nations. Samoa has competed at every <a href="/wiki/Rugby_World_Cup" title="Rugby World Cup">Rugby World Cup</a> since <a href="/wiki/1991_Rugby_World_Cup" title="1991 Rugby World Cup">1991</a>, and made the quarter finals in 1991, <a href="/wiki/1995_Rugby_World_Cup" title="1995 Rugby World Cup">1995</a> and the second round of the <a href="/wiki/1999_Rugby_World_Cup" title="1999 Rugby World Cup">1999</a> World Cup.<sup id="cite_ref-97" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-97">[97]</a></sup> At the 2003 world cup, Manu Samoa came close to beating eventual world champions, England. Samoa also played in the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Nations_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="Pacific Nations Cup">Pacific Nations Cup</a> and the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Tri-Nations" title="Pacific Tri-Nations">Pacific Tri-Nations</a>. The sport is governed by the <a href="/wiki/Samoa_Rugby_Football_Union" class="mw-redirect" title="Samoa Rugby Football Union">Samoa Rugby Football Union</a>, who are members of the <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islands_Rugby_Alliance" title="Pacific Islands Rugby Alliance">Pacific Islands Rugby Alliance</a>, and thus, also contribute to the international <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Islanders_rugby_union_team" title="Pacific Islanders rugby union team">Pacific Islanders rugby union team</a>. </p>
      <p>At club level, there is the <a href="/wiki/Samoa_National_Provincial_Championship" title="Samoa National Provincial Championship">National Provincial Championship</a> and <a href="/wiki/Pacific_Rugby_Cup" class="mw-redirect" title="Pacific Rugby Cup">Pacific Rugby Cup</a>. They also took home the cup at Wellington and the Hong Kong Rugby Sevens in 2007—for which the Prime Minister of Samoa, also Chairman of the national rugby union, Tuila’epa Sa’ilele Malielegaoi, declared a national holiday. They were also the <a href="/wiki/IRB_World_Sevens_Series" class="mw-redirect" title="IRB World Sevens Series">IRB World Sevens Series</a> Champions in 2010 capping a year of achievement for the Samoans, following wins in the US, Australia, Hong Kong and Scotland Sevens tournaments. </p>
      <p>Prominent Samoan players include <a href="/wiki/Pat_Lam" title="Pat Lam">Pat Lam</a> and <a href="/wiki/Brian_Lima" title="Brian Lima">Brian Lima</a>. In addition, many Samoans have played for or are playing for <a href="/wiki/New_Zealand_national_rugby_union_team" title="New Zealand national rugby union team">New Zealand</a>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/Rugby_league" title="Rugby league">Rugby league</a> is mostly played by Samoans living in New Zealand and Australia.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (August 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> <a href="/wiki/Samoa_national_rugby_league_team" title="Samoa national rugby league team">Samoa</a> reached the quarter finals of the <a href="/wiki/2013_Rugby_League_World_Cup" title="2013 Rugby League World Cup">2013 Rugby League World Cup</a>, the team comprising players from the <a href="/wiki/NRL" class="mw-redirect" title="NRL">NRL</a> and <a href="/wiki/Super_League" title="Super League">Super League</a> plus domestic players. Many Samoans and New Zealanders or Australians of Samoan descent play in the Super League and National Leagues in Britain, including Francis Meli, Ta'ane Lavulavu of Workington Town, Maurie Fa'asavalu of St Helens, David Fatialofa of Whitehaven and Setaimata Sa, who signed with London Irish rugby club. Other noteworthy players from NZ and Australia have represented the <a href="/wiki/Samoa_national_rugby_league_team" title="Samoa national rugby league team">Samoan National team</a>. The 2011 domestic Samoan rugby league competition contained 10 teams with plans to expand to 12 in 2012.<sup id="cite_ref-Rugby_League_Planet_98-0" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-Rugby_League_Planet-98">[98]</a></sup><sup id="cite_ref-99" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-99">[99]</a></sup> </p>
      <p>Samoans have been very visible in <a href="/wiki/Boxing" title="Boxing">boxing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Kickboxing" title="Kickboxing">kickboxing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Professional_wrestling" title="Professional wrestling">wrestling</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Sumo" title="Sumo">sumo</a>; some Samoan sumo wrestlers, most famously <a href="/wiki/Musashimaru" class="mw-redirect" title="Musashimaru">Musashimaru</a> and <a href="/wiki/Konishiki" class="mw-redirect" title="Konishiki">Konishiki</a>, have reached the highest rank of <i><a href="/wiki/Oozeki" class="mw-redirect" title="Oozeki">Ozeki</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Yokozuna_(sumo)" class="mw-redirect" title="Yokozuna (sumo)">yokozuna</a></i>. </p>
      <p><a href="/wiki/American_football" title="American football">American football</a> is occasionally played in Samoa, reflecting its wide popularity in <a href="/wiki/American_Samoa" title="American Samoa">American Samoa</a>, where the sport is played under high school sanction. About 30 ethnic Samoans, many from American Samoa, currently play in the <a href="/wiki/National_Football_League" title="National Football League">National Football League</a>. A 2002 article from <i><a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a></i> estimated that a Samoan male (either an American Samoan or a Samoan living in the mainland United States) is 40 times more likely to play in the NFL than a non-Samoan American.<sup id="cite_ref-100" class="reference"><a href="#cite_note-100">[100]</a></sup> </p> 
      <h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Samoa&amp;action=edit&amp;section=29" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2> 
      <style data-mw-deduplicate="TemplateStyles:r936637989">.mw-parser-output .portal{border:solid #aaa 1px;padding:0}.mw-parser-output .portal.tleft{margin:0.5em 1em 0.5em 0}.mw-parser-output .portal.tright{margin:0.5em 0 0.5em 1em}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul{display:table;box-sizing:border-box;padding:0.1em;max-width:175px;background:#f9f9f9;font-size:85%;line-height:110%;font-style:italic;font-weight:bold}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li{display:table-row}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li>span:first-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em;vertical-align:middle;text-align:center}.mw-parser-output .portal>ul>li>span:last-child{display:table-cell;padding:0.2em 0.2em 0.2em 0.3em;vertical-align:middle}</style>
      <div role="navigation" aria-label="Portals" class="noprint portal plainlist tright"> 
       <ul> 
        <li><span><a href="/wiki/File:%E5%A4%A7%E6%B4%8B.png" class="image"><img alt="icon" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/%E5%A4%A7%E6%B4%8B.png/32px-%E5%A4%A7%E6%B4%8B.png" decoding="async" width="32" height="26" class="noviewer" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/%E5%A4%A7%E6%B4%8B.png/48px-%E5%A4%A7%E6%B4%8B.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/7/7b/%E5%A4%A7%E6%B4%8B.png/64px-%E5%A4%A7%E6%B4%8B.png 2x" data-file-width="756" data-file-height="617"></a></span><span><a href="/wiki/Portal:Oceania" title="Portal:Oceania">Oceania portal</a></span></li>
       </ul>
      </div>
